    <li> I&#x27;ve been using it for seven months. It does the job, but multi-blade razors are superior. I have a big goatee, and only shave my cheeks, I don&#x27;t have a full beard because the sides are soft and too sparse, yet many passes are needed, and the blades wear out fast.     <li> A bit to get used to, more so than a commercial disposable blade type. Smooth shave and I didn&#x27;t cut my throat, success!</li>
    <li> I have some facial hair and I dislike the pain of tweezing.  My hair is very coarse so waxing isn&#x27;t a good option for me either.  The cost of 5-6 blades for plastic razors is outrageous and while looking for another option, I found the micro touch safety razor.  I was a 20 year user of the personal touch razor until they discontinued it. (sigh) Been using this razor for 5 mos.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) The Razor.  Looks nice, chrome top and handle and comes with a little stand to suspend it upright on the counter.  The stand is fine if working at the sink, it would not work in the shower unless you have a special or built in shelf to support it. The handle is very short, about 3 1/4 inches, a little small for ladies but you get used to it. Blades can be changed easily with a twist of the handle to open the head.  **In the 5th month, the twist bottom was stuck, had to use a pair of pliers to open it. I think it was a due to over tightening the handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) Usage.  Not that difficult to get used to, I normally have a light touch with the razors--especially on my face so there was little to no learning curve for me--DO NOT SCRAPE against the skin or you will be left with an unsightly knick.  Be sure to warm the area with water and shaving foam or soap before use.  Also, shaving with the grain of the hair growth first, then against it produces the best, smoothest result for me.  When I say smooth, I mean it.  It looks and feels like I have no hair growth at all.  I also have found that the results of this shave last longer for whatever reason meaning I don&#x27;t have to shave every day (as I did with a regular razor) and instead find every couple of days to suffice.  Frankly, with the use of this razor, I no longer get &#x27;stressed&#x27; at the thought of someone touching my face...which makes me very happy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I&#x27;m very pleased with the performance of this piece and plan to keep it until it is no longer usable or I die.  Whichever comes first.  If its the former, I&#x27;ll def by another.     <li> It will work reasonably well IF you do good prep (shaving lather made with a brush from shaving soap or shaving cream, and not canned foam) and try a variety of brands of blades to see which one(s) work for you---and this razor works best with a sharper blade, like a Feather, Astra Superior Platinum, Gillette 7 O&#x27;Clock SharpEdge, Voskhod, Personna Lab Blue, or the like. (The reason that blade sampler packs are so common is that the same brand of blade will work great for one guy and be horrible for another---thus each shaver must experiment to discover which brand(s) work for him. And a brand that&#x27;s best in one razor may not be best (or even good) in another, so the exploration must be done for each razor.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Still, there are MUCH better razors for the novice.     <li> For people who have been used to the safety razors or multi-blade razors this item may throw you for a curve, but I have to say it is worth the purchase and time to learn to use it.  As a shaver who grew up in the era when multi-bladed razors gained dominance I used disposable single/double bladed razors for a significant time while I was in the military.  They were cheap, dependable, and required no maintenance.  Later I made the switch to the multi-bladed razors with replaceable heads.  Again they were dependable and required little maintenance (though hair clogging happened often) but these were far from cheap.  Prices soon climbed to more than $20 for a pack of 4 blades at local retailers.  I wasn&#x27;t ready to invest a significant portion of time buying the blades online or shopping around for the best price so I switched back to disposables for the past few years.&lt;br /&gt;At one point my father-in-law suggested this product (not specifically, but a classic razor with disposable blades like how &amp;#34;he used to shave&amp;#34;).  I have seen the Rick Harrison commercial once before so I decided to make the buy.  I have to admit that if you are unfamiliar with using this type of razor it can seem daunting, but basic principals still apply.  Shave with the grain and use a roughly 45 degree angle.  The really key is the amount of pressure you use, people used to safety razors and multi-blades know you can put quite a bit of force on your face with no worries.  Don&#x27;t do that here.  This is delicate instrument compared to the more brutish disposables.  Let the weight of the razor pull and you&#x27;ll be fine.  I was a bit concerned that there was some tugging as I shaved, but when i switched from a shaving gel to an actual foam (a cheap Barbasol foam worked very well in fact) it went away for the most part.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Verdict:&lt;br /&gt;This razor is worth it.  In fact I think any of the Classic Safety Razors is worth a try if you are as fed up with blade prices as I am.  This razor gives me as good of a shave as any multi-blade I have ever used and I can get a pack of 50 replaceable blades for around $10.  You will have to put in the time to learn how the razor works and you may need to change the way you shave or what other products you might use when shaving, but its a small price to pay to be clean shaven and a bit wealthier.s me as good of a shave as any multi-blade I have ever used and I can get a pack of 50 replaceable blades for around $10. After learning to reduce the stubble through multiple light passes with this razor, those other razors feel like a hack and go option. The hack and go method would leave my face feeling raw, create ingrown hairs, and made shaving a dreaded process.     <li> This razor is a great one for the price. It took some getting used too with the short handle, but it works. I won&#x27;t shave with anything other than the Micro Touch now because the blades for it are dirt cheap. You can get a pack of 100 Derby Extra blades on Amazon for about $10. Since this is my first DE safety razor it took a little bit of experimenting to keep from cutting myself repeatedly.   You will notice on this razor that there are 2 sides with different levels of blade exposure. I kept using the side with the wider gap (more blade exposure) and was cutting myself nearly every time I shaved!!!! Big mistake... You only want to use that side if you have more facial hair to cut down. It is not for the finishing strokes. Since I have switched over to the side with less blade exposure my skin gets a lot less irritated and I have not cut myself once. I usually shave in the bathtub which helps to prevent irritation and cuts since the blade is in constant contact with hot water and soap. It is a great way too. Just keep your face covered in hot water and soap with every pass and you will be fine. Highly recommended buy if you want to save money.</li>

    <li> For quite some time now, I&#x27;ve been fed up with the cost of name brand &amp;#34;modern&amp;#34; razors like the Gillette Fusions.  It always amazed me how expensive they were compared to how long they lasted (not very).  I would notice a decline in shave quality by 5-6 shaves, typically...however, wanting to stretch my dollar as far as possible, I would refuse to change the blade until I had used it about double that amount, and the razor was to the point I couldn&#x27;t stand it anymore.  This created an endless cycle of harsh, unsatisfying shaves, and so my search began for a better way.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I tried Dorco&#x27;s equivalent razor, not bad at all considering how much cheaper it was, but I still wasn&#x27;t totally satisfied for the same reasons I was unsatisfied with Fusions.  I was about to try a second discount brand of multi-blade cartridges, but in my quest of finding a better, more cost effective way to shave, I learned about the old school method of using a double-edge safety razor.  Almost everything I read about it told me the same thing, that once people made the switch, almost everyone found it a much better, more comfortable way to shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My mom, being the kind hearted person she is, ordered this razor for me after I mentioned wanting to try it.  I also picked up an inexpensive Tweezerman shaving brush, and some old fashioned shaving cream in a tub.  So my journey towards a better shaving experience began.  It didn&#x27;t take long, as I was a convert after the first couple of shaves.  The razor itself is very comfortable to hold, easy to load blades into, and in general is very forgiving if you&#x27;re new to DE shaving, as I was.  There is definitely a learning curve, and the first few shaves are typically not the best, however the real payoff comes from sticking with it and taking the extra time needed to learn proper technique and blade angle when shaving.  Once you have that down, you&#x27;ll be rewarded with a great, comfortable shave.  If you get this, I highly recommend you go for the full &amp;#34;classic&amp;#34; shaving setup with a shaving brush and traditional shaving cream or soap in order to get the most out of this razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The reason why I only gave it 4 stars, ironically, is the same reason why it&#x27;s great for beginners.  This razor has a very small blade exposure, and while it makes it a forgiving razor, it&#x27;s a little too mild for my beard.  I have thick, course facial hair and I have to often go over the same spot multiple times to get the level of closeness I want (I usually do the &amp;#34;classic&amp;#34; 3-pass method, and then touch-ups).  I can usually get baby smooth on my cheeks, but the neck area still leaves something to be desired.  Again, this is just a matter of how the razor pairs with my beard; it might be perfect for someone with lighter hair growth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall I am very satisfied with this razor and would recommend it to anyone looking for a better shave experience.  I do plan to eventually upgrade to a more aggressive safety razor, but I feel this was an excellent starting point while I learned the new techniques.  Don&#x27;t be alarmed by the initial investment cost (razor, brush, cream), as this will actually save money in the long run since traditional shaving cream lasts for ages (a fingernail-sized amount will make enough lather for a full shave) and the replacement DE blades typically cost 1/10 or less than a multi-blade cartridge.  Your face will definitely thank you.</li>

    <li> When seeking product reviews, I always read the worst reviews first thus giving me the hypeless product lowdown. I am in my 50s and have been using single blade style safety razors since I was 19. My main shavers are fancy (and expensive) Edwin Jagger ($45.00) and The Art of Shaving ($95.00) handles using the Merkur German blades.     <li> Have been using safety razors for many years and I have to say that this razor gives me a shave equal to my Merkur and Jagger razors. Seems decently made and holds the blades in alignment and tightly. Take it from an old hand with these type of razors, get yourself a good badger hair brush and a nicely scented cake soap. Don&#x27;t use canned shave cream with these razors, they will dry out your skin and will not give you a comfortable experience. The cake type soaps will lubricate your face and makes the razor literally glide over the skin. Also get yourself a variety pack of blades here on Amazon, not all blades are created equal and you&#x27;ll end up finding the brand that works best for you. Using a safety razor had become almost a lost art form, but they seem to be making a comeback, probably due to the cost of quality disposables. I won&#x27;t ever trade my safety razors for anything else.&lt;br /&gt;  I have noticed many reviews on not only this but other DE razors from folks saying how badly they have gotten cut up. There is a trick to using a DE razor and getting the best shave from them. Since they have no swiveling or tilting head you will need to learn to hold the razor at the proper angle that is best for your type of beard thru out the stroke. Also, use multiple short strokes instead of long ones like you would with the new multi-blades. Also if your older or have looser skin on your neck, you need to pull or stretch the skin a little in order for the razor to get as close as possible. Shave in the direction of the hair growth first, rinse and re-lather, then shave again against the grain. Don&#x27;t think you can pull a DE razor out and just start swiping away, BIG mistake. When you load the blade into the razor, especially if it&#x27;s a butterfly style, watch  when you close the head against the blade. The blade will shift slightly. Close the razor until the doors just start to apply a little pressure on the blade, then adjust the blade in all directions so you have equal blade edge exposed on both sides then tighten the rest of the way. Take your time and you will learn to get a very nice shave at a fraction of the cost of the multi-blades.edge exposed on both sides then tighten the rest of the way. Take your time and you will learn to get a very nice shave at a fraction of the cost of the multi-blades.</li>

    <li> I bought this razor for $20, including 12 blades and a chrome stand, and I must say that I am very satisfied with it.  After years of trying Braun, Norelco, Remington and Panasonic electric razors, I have used disposable twin blade razors for the last few years, anything without a lubricating strip (that irritates my skin and takes away the traction that I personally need to get a good, close shave).  I saw the infomercial and thought I would give this a try, remembering the old Gillette twist-to-open DE razor that my Dad used when I was very little (1970&#x27;s).  While everyone&#x27;s face and beard growth/density is different, this works great for me.  I prefer to use Shave Secret shaving oil (or sometimes even just hot water), rather than the soap, brush, and mug that most DE shavers use.  A lot of reviewers mention the proper shave method (vital if you are going to enjoy this razor), build quality of the razor, sharpness of the blades, etc.  I am going to cover a few things that I have not seen mentioned (or coverd in detail).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. A lot of folks are surprised that an old-fashioned DE razor can shave as close (or closer) than a multi-blade disposable razor (or cartridge).  I believe one of the reasons is the double-bevel edge of a DE razor blade.  All three types of disposable razors in our household (under magnification) clearly have only a single-bevel edge (from the top).  I am not sure whether DE (double edge) blades are called that because they have two cutting edges (where you spin your razor around 180 degrees and use the other edge) or because they are sharpened/honed from the top and bottom of the blade.  I do know that it makes for a sharper edge, and that is why you can get such a close shave with DE blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. The thing that dulls a blade the most is actually oxidation of the cutting edge.  For this reason, when I took out my first blade (that I am still on after 7 shaves), I carefully smeared a tiny drop of Shave Secret oil on the top andbottom of it before letting it touch any water (NOT smearing in the direction to get cut).  I also do the same as I clean up after each shave, using Shave Secret as an aftershave too.  As far as I can tell, my blade is still just as sharp as when I started using it.  I am sure that mineral oil would work just as well for preventing oxidation of the blade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3.  Cleanup is SO much easier with this style of razor.  There are actually openings all underneath the blade to allow for easy cleaning, and I have noticed that a fast pumping up and down in hot water cleans the blade very well.  I saw another reviewer who said they have often broken their plastic razors while tapping them firmly against the sink, and I have had the exact same experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. While this is not an adjustable DE razor, (using CAUTION) you can make it shave a little closer for your final pass (or make it shave a little more aggressively all the time).  If you look through the side of the razor as you tighten a blade in, you can see how it &amp;#34;bows&amp;#34; the blade up into a curve right as it starts to max out, setting up the angle at which this razor was meant to shave at.  If it is tightened all the way, then backed off even a TINY amount, it will set the blade at a more aggressive angle for shaving (but use caution and make sure you still see it bowed from the side).  I have found that if I loosen it until the blade is seen to be bowed halfway, it makes for a closer shave (and easier cuts if you are not careful).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Happy shaving!  And remember to give it a few shaves and learn the proper technique for shaving this way.  You will be glad you did.</li>
    <li> Thank you Rick Harrison.</li>

    <li> Safety Razors are the Best Way to get a clean smooth shave. Here is how I get the best shave:&lt;br /&gt;Wet the face with warm water, make sure your face is feeling warm. A warm wash cloth works best. While you have the warm water running close the drain slightly so you have some hot water in the sink. Place your razor in the warm water to heat the blade. Having the blade warm is a huge part of getting a close shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Place a few drops of Shave Secret in your palm and rub your hand slightly to get it even then apply to your warm face. Work the oil in and be ready to shave. I start at my left temple and move down in small strokes with the grain of my beard. Be sure to swish the razor in the sinks warm water to clean the blade. I hold the end of the handle to let the shavers weight set the pressure against my skin. Keep the shaver at a 45 degree to the skin. Pull your skin tight for the closest shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Feel for areas you may have missed but be sure to press hard with the shaver or it will cut you.&lt;br /&gt;I find I get about two shaves out of one side of the razor blade before I flip it or switch it out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will never go back to disposables! Try it, all you have to loose it a little blood.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been using the Micro Touch Safety Razor for about three months now. I almost gave this product three stars, but just before writing this review, I decided to inspect my razor closer and noticed I could no longer open the top anymore (by twisting the handle) to replace the blades, which are all a little dull and rough by the way. I&#x27;m guessing this is due to rust build up on the inside. I had to use a pair of pliers to twist the top lids open (and cut myself twice doing it). I had read in the reviews where other customers complained about the same thing. I was hoping that was a rare fluke, but I guess not. Also, when this razor first arrived in the mail, I noticed a small chip in the silver plating on the neck, which was a little disappointing. I also noticed on the first day that one of the butterfly flaps (that&#x27;s what I call them), where the blade is installed, wouldn&#x27;t go all the way down. I sort of didn&#x27;t mind that, though, because it always helped me to know what side I had been using. After using one side for a long while, I would switch to the other freshly sharpened side. I had never used a safety razor before, other than playing with my dad&#x27;s safety razor when I was a boy, but I got the hang of it very quickly. You just have to be a little more gentle and careful. I think I nicked myself only about 3 or 4 times, since I&#x27;ve had it. I should also add that many have complained about the short handle, but I like the shorter handle because I was able to quickly switch the angle of the razor and move it around within my hand without a long handle getting in my way.     <li> I have used Gillette Sensor (and later, Mach 3) blades since I started shaving, 23 years ago.  They both do a great job, but the price of the Mach 3 blades has gotten out of control. I can&#x27;t see myself going back to the Mach 3 or any other type of razor.  The trick with this razor is to take your time and don&#x27;t use very much pressure.  Shave with the grain, first, and then if you have to shave against the grain, re-lather and use short, gentle, upstrokes.  It takes some practice, but you will get the hang of it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only gripe I have is that the handle is extremely short.  Not good for someone like me that has bigger hands.     <li> Ever looking for the safest and most comfortable way to shave, I ordered a Microtouch One razor when I saw it advertised on TV. I should have done some research first because it turned out to be a mistake. My first observation has to do with quality. At the price of $19.95 and up I&#x27;d expect it to be at least good if not excellent. But close inspection of the item reveals a cheap rehash of an old classic, probably manufactured in China at bargain rates to the distributor (who no doubt is making a killing in the spread). My second point is that the bulky design makes it a difficult item to handle in some parts of the face, such us under the nose or where the neck joins the jaw. (These are places that a modern disposable easily navigates.) But the most dissatisfying issue with this product is the &amp;#34;safety&amp;#34; factor. These types of razors were probably dubbed &amp;#34;safety&amp;#34; razors when compared to a barber&#x27;s super sharp open switch blade, but they are not all that safe compared to today&#x27;s modern disposables or not so disposables. I shaved with the Microtouch three times (twice more than I really wanted to but wanted to give it a fair try) and finally conceded that I had been duped (ripped off). All three shaves were uncomfortable, worrisome (it always felt like there was too much razor blade exposed to the skin) and, in fact, I did cut myself once despite being careful not to. In short, there was nothing comfortable to using a Microtouch and I really do get much closer and more comfortable shaves from my disposables. I do not recommend the Microtouch product. Only those who are married to the idea of using a classic design, despite the discomfort and safety concerns, could enjoy this product.</li>

    <li> Excellent. I&#x27;ll buy this again!</li>
    <li> After watching a TV commercial exposing the merits of the old fashion double edge razor as I had grown up shaving with, I decided to shun the expensive Gillette Mach razors and go back to the basics.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Now I know it has been 45 years since I had used a DE razor so I had to reeducate myself in my shaving techniques such as softening the bearded area by using soap and hot water.  Also shaving lightly with the grain letting the weight of the razor to glide down and capture all the bearded areas.  Also a light second shaving lightly against the grain was needed for a close shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; However due to the cheapness of this product several problems emerged to prevent a close, clean and bloodless shave.&lt;br /&gt;1. This razor is not an exact precision instrument.  It is not built on a slight angle to capture the beard without scraping.  Angled at 45 degrees it is a scrapper and with this razor being so light the blade drags against the skin and will cause nicks and cuts.  It is a bleeding razor.&lt;br /&gt;2. The razor after being used for about a month became hard to open and in fact I had to use pliers to open the butterfly blade opening.  Very cheaply made.&lt;br /&gt;3.
